<div id="review_931437162" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/931437162" />
    <a title="Liviania" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1430644-liviania"><img alt="Liviania" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1218840926p2/1430644.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/931437162?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liviania" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liviania" href="/user/show/1430644-liviania">Liviania</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer931437162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13257070473290103398">Cousins Mariko Tamaki and Jillian Tamaki brilliantly capture the liminal time between being a teenager and being a child in their new graphic novel, THIS ONE SUMMER. Rose and Windy are friends who hang out every summer when their families visit Awago Beach. They like swimming and buying candy and renting R-rated videos, which they can get away with since the teenage clerk doesn't really care.<br/><br/>They're at the age where they're starting to clue into things like sex jokes, but don't really understand</span>
  <span id="freeText13257070473290103398" style="display:none">Cousins Mariko Tamaki and Jillian Tamaki brilliantly capture the liminal time between being a teenager and being a child in their new graphic novel, THIS ONE SUMMER. Rose and Windy are friends who hang out every summer when their families visit Awago Beach. They like swimming and buying candy and renting R-rated videos, which they can get away with since the teenage clerk doesn't really care.<br /><br />They're at the age where they're starting to clue into things like sex jokes, but don't really understand them. Their hormones are starting to go a bit wild, causing both crushes and anger. They're still kids, but their actions are starting to carry deeper consequences.<br /><br />Although Rose and Windy are young, THIS ONE SUMMER is best enjoyed by a reader who is at least slightly older. The real treat is putting together what Rose and Windy notice into the whole story. Some is gathered through Mariko's script, and other clues are only in Jillian's art, such as Rose's mom's defensive, hunched in body language.<br /><br />There are some genuinely disturbing moments, of the mundanely disturbing type. A family friend violates Rose's mom's boundaries, and Rose doesn't get it because she just wants her mom to have fun and her mom is refusing to. She doesn't understand her mom's motives and isn't old enough to suss them out. Meanwhile, Rose also shows that she's picked up a real misogynistic streak from the teenage boys hanging around the corner store, which drives a wedge between her and Windy. It's painfully real, that difficultly of growing into being a teenage girl while being taught to hate those other girls who aren't like you.<br /><br />There's a beautiful, and beautifully complicated thread of family running through THIS ONE SUMMER. Rose and Windy are like sisters. Rose's parents tried for another child, but didn't have one. Windy is adopted. A local teenage girl is pregnant, and only has a few people offering her any support. The relationships are as complicated as enjoying a swim on the beautiful beach is easy, and Rose and Windy are caught between those worlds.<br /><br />THIS ONE SUMMER is a lovely slice of life novel that perfectly captures the wonders of summer and a transitional time of life. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13257070473290103398" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2148014575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3641268546938107736">Rose spends her summer's at a beach house with her family. She meets Windy there every year and they hang out. This summer her mom is depressed. Rose spends her days listening to local gossip, renting horror movies and hanging out with Windy. <br/><br/>There are funny moments when they have a dance party or they are talking about growing boobs.   <span id="freeText3641268546938107736" style="display:none">Rose spends her summer's at a beach house with her family. She meets Windy there every year and they hang out. This summer her mom is depressed. Rose spends her days listening to local gossip, renting horror movies and hanging out with Windy. <br /><br />There are funny moments when they have a dance party or they are talking about growing boobs. There are serious moments when an older teen finds she is pregnant or her mom spending her days on the couch.<br /><br />This book is simple and it pulls on your summer memories of hanging out and doing nothing or whatever you wanted. I never got to have a beach house and I remember simply hanging around outside watching the world go by. I really enjoyed this book. It was a quiet book really and it had volumes to say in quiet ways. The art is fairly colorless and maybe that somehow adds to the feeling of it being a memory or something, just a little faded and there at the same time. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bqxI12j8yYwA5v8KBhV0eIaNU4aeupb84SG5gN8H+T8ilU5/zZlAXBDE/EV2nXVNRZuTc67S+iJE8UhR4UsusQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('V1tcPMJQTxoTIE9hHjpjKKxdfRFEuXwleJ8mGk6YHGQbYlqUZzXGygMCTC5usmIdb0u95HTREPvdT9fLcNTL6g==')})
  }
//]]>

She’s from Atlanta, she’s never kissed a guy, she’s into Backstreet Boys in a really deep way, and her long summer days are full of a pleasant, peaceful nothing . . . until one confounding moment. A split-second of innocent physical contact pulls Maggie into a gut-twisting love for an older, wiser, and most surprising of all (at least to Maggie), female counselor named Erin. But Camp Bellflower is an impossible place for a girl to fall in love with another girl, and Maggie’s savant-like proficiency at the camp’s rifle range is the only thing keeping her heart from exploding. When it seems as if Erin maybe feels the same way about Maggie, it’s too much for both Maggie and Camp Bellflower to handle, let alone to understand.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"7597648988365874860\"       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/483588.Mariko_Tamaki">About Mariko Tamaki</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/483588.Mariko_Tamaki"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1387259250p3/483588.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/483588.Mariko_Tamaki">Mariko Tamaki
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,240
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11559783682704149564">Mariko Tamaki is a Toronto writer, playwright, activist and performer. She works and performs with fat activists Pretty Porky and Pissed Off and the theatre troupe TOA, whose recent play, <i>A vs. B</i>, was staged at the 2004 Rhubarb Festival at Buddies in Bad Times Theatre. Her well-received novel, <i>Cover Me</i> (McGilligan Books) was followed by a short fiction collection, <i>True Lies: The Book of Bad Advice</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11559783682704149564" style="display:none">Mariko Tamaki is a Toronto writer, playwright, activist and performer. She works and performs with fat activists Pretty Porky and Pissed Off and the theatre troupe TOA, whose recent play, <i>A vs. B</i>, was staged at the 2004 Rhubarb Festival at Buddies in Bad Times Theatre. Her well-received novel, <i>Cover Me</i> (McGilligan Books) was followed by a short fiction collection, <i>True Lies: The Book of Bad Advice</i> (Women's Press). Mariko's third book, <i>FAKE ID</i>, is due out in spring 2005.<br /><br />Mariko Tamaki has performed her work across Canada and through the States, recently appearing at the Calgary Folkfest 2004, Vancouver Writer's Festival 2003, Spatial III, and the Perpetual Motion/Girls Bite Back Tour, which circled though Ottawa, Montreal, Brooklyn and Chicago. She has appeared widely on radio and television including First Person Singular on CBC radio and Imprint on TVO. Mariko Tamaki is currently attending York University working a master's degree in women's studies.<br /><br />[MacMIllan Books]</span>
  <a data-text-id="11559783682704149564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
